          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          across different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
          critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
          disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
          architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
          base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring

      response:
        output: ' Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the regulation of expression across various conditions, a realization crucial for therapy development. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated individual gene roles in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions are pivotal to disease onset and progression. Here, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally essential genes lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations through co-expressed gene groups, revealing potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations via the lens of gene modules, thereby enhancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: ' In the context of complex traits and diseases, genes often act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their functions. A mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across different conditions is crucial for uncovering gene-gene interactions that influence complex traits and developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, but modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in disease origin and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

      response:
        output: >2-
           In a concerted manner, genes interact with one another within specific contexts to perform their functions. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the regulation of expression across diverse conditions. This insight is pivotal for the development of new therapeutic approaches. Transcriptome-wide association studies have aided in uncovering the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions are crucial for disease origin and progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We discover that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
          therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex traits

        output: >2-
           Understanding the interplay of genes in specific contexts is essential for elucidating their roles in complex traits, which is crucial for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on individual gene functions in disease mechanisms, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions are vital in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          about the importance of understanding gene interactions in complex
          traits for developing new therapies. It also retains the content about
          PhenoPLIER's computational approach, latent representation, and
          application to gene-trait associations. Finally, it emphasizes the
          conclusion that PhenoPLIER can reveal potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies, providing a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through gene modules, thereby highlighting
          disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

This insight is crucial for developing innovative therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped elucidate the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations through the lens of gene co-expression modules, revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. This novel framework offers a powerful tool for interpreting genetic associations and understanding disease mechanisms from a functional genomics perspective.'

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

While transcriptome-wide association studies have uncovered the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies, providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

           Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits requires insight into expression regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is vital for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings show that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER incorporates groups of co-expressed genes, contextualizing genetic associations and revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, illuminating disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

Genes function in coordination with one another in specific contexts to carry out their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across various conditions, which is essential for the development of novel therapies. Traditional transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the individual gene contributions to disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are crucial in determining disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER''s representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We discover significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can provide context to genetic associations and reveal potential targets that may be overlooked in single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, facilitating insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes

          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with

          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

           We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for collaborative analysis. Genes function in concert within specific contexts to perform their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the regulation of expression across different conditions, which is essential for developing novel therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have illuminated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms, contemporary models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on groups of genes with similar expression patterns under identical conditions. We discover that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally critical players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, by incorporating co-expressed gene groups, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and identifies potential targets previously missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for decoding genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

However, current research has primarily focused on single-gene strategies, which may not capture the complex interactions between genes that play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Our method identifies groups of co-expressed genes, which are significantly associated with diseases in relevant cell types. We demonstrate the accuracy of our approach in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, contextualizing these associations and revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. This approach has the potential to advance our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms, ultimately contributing to the development of more effective therapeutic targets and repurposing of existing drugs.'

           We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint analysis. Understanding how genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions is crucial for elucidating the influence of these genes on complex traits. This knowledge is vital for discovering novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms, but current models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in the origin and progression of diseases. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on gene modules with similar expression patterns across various conditions. We find that diseases are significantly correlated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Utilizing a CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we discover that functionally critical elements lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, shedding light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          usage.

          simplifies the language and emphasizes the integration aspect of
          PhenoPLIER's approach.

          language in the abstract.

          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies." with "In

          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets

          significance of the findings and strengthens the concluding statement.

          grammatical adjustment enhances the clarity of the abstract's
          language.

          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          significance").

While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. Our study demonstrates that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in pertinent cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Utilizing a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally relevant players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER presents a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, shedding light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms in functional genomics studies.

          Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
          therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex traits

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

           In the field of functional genomics, genes interact with one another in specific contexts to carry out their functions. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across diverse conditions. This insight is critical for the development of novel therapies. In our study, we demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. By employing a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, integrating groups of co-expressed genes with PhenoPLIER enables the contextualization of genetic associations and reveals potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, providing a significant advancement in understanding disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          In this research paper titled "Projecting genetic associations through
          gene expression patterns highlights disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms," we have investigated the role of co-expressed genes in
          determining complex traits and their potential as therapeutic targets.
          The study focuses on functional genomics, specifically exploring the
          connections between gene modules and their relevance to disease and
          drug mechanisms.


          Our methodology involves a comprehensive analysis of gene expression
          patterns across different conditions to gain insights into how genes
          work together in specific contexts. We have employed advanced
          techniques such as CRISPR screens to analyze lipid regulation and
          identify functionally important players that may not necessarily have
          strong associations but are crucial for understanding the underlying
          mechanisms.


          Our results show that diseases are significantly associated with gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types, indicating a strong
          relationship between gene expression patterns and disease progression.
          Additionally, our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease

          processes. Moreover, the use of PhenoPLIER, a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          allows us to contextualize these associations and identify potential
          targets that might be missed using single-gene strategies.

          by highlighting the importance of gene co-expression in disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms. The findings suggest that incorporating
          groups of co-expressed genes can provide a more comprehensive
          understanding of genetic associations and help uncover previously
          overlooked therapeutic targets. This research not only fills a gap in
          current knowledge but also has broader implications for the
          development of new therapies and our comprehension of complex traits.

          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific

This knowledge is essential for developing targeted therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, modern complex trait architecture models suggest that gene-gene interactions play pivotal roles in disease origins and progression.            Genetic studies have provided valuable insights into the etiology of complex diseases and the mechanisms of action for drugs. However, understanding gene-gene interactions in the context of gene expression patterns remains a significant challenge. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across different conditions. We demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using CRISPR screening to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, our work highlights the importance of considering gene co-expression in genetic studies, shedding light on therapeutic targets and facilitating drug repurposing efforts.

          In this paper, we address a critical gap in the literature regarding
          the integration of gene-gene interactions with gene expression
          patterns to better understand disease etiology and drug mechanisms. We
          present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          different conditions. Through extensive evaluation, we show that our
          approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Moreover, using CRISPR screening to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack

          PhenoPLIER. Our work has significant implications for the field of
          genetic studies, as it underscores the importance of gene
          co-expression and its role in elucidating therapeutic targets and
          facilitating drug repurposing efforts.

          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,

          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

        output: ' Genes interact with one another in specific contexts to carry out their functions, and understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a comprehensive understanding of expression regulation across diverse conditions. This insight is essential for the development of novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have facilitated the identification of individual genes'' roles in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits propose that gene-gene interactions are crucial in determining the origin and progression of diseases. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on groups of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Moreover, utilizing a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.'

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific

          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of

          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.

          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly

          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players

        output: ' In the field of genetics, understanding how genes work together in specific contexts is crucial for determining their influence on complex traits. This knowledge is essential for developing new therapies and uncovering disease-relevant mechanisms. Although transcriptome-wide association studies have provided valuable insights into individual gene roles, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across different conditions. Our results demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lacking associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, this study highlights the potential of PhenoPLIER as a powerful tool for understanding gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, and drug repurposing in the context of complex traits.'

Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the regulation of expression across various conditions, a realization crucial for therapy development. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated individual gene roles in disease-related mechanisms.             text: ' In the context of complex traits and diseases, genes often act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their functions. A mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across different conditions is crucial for uncovering gene-gene interactions that influence complex traits and developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped identify the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, but modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in disease origin and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

              ---
               In a concerted manner, genes interact with one another within specific contexts to perform their functions. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the regulation of expression across diverse conditions. This insight is pivotal for the development of new therapeutic approaches. Transcriptome-wide association studies have aided in uncovering the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions are crucial for disease origin and progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We discover that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering
              of complex traits

               Understanding the interplay of genes in specific contexts is essential for elucidating their roles in complex traits, which is crucial for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on individual gene functions in disease mechanisms, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions are vital in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              ---
               Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits requires insight into expression regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is vital for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings show that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER incorporates groups of co-expressed genes, contextualizing genetic associations and revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, illuminating disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering

              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps

              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This

              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules.

            text: ' Genes function in concert within specific contexts to perform their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a comprehensive understanding of expression regulation across diverse conditions. This knowledge is essential for the development of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped elucidate the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease initiation and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally crucial players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by integrating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can provide context to genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

              ---
               We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for comprehensive analysis. Genes function in coordination with one another in specific contexts to carry out their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across various conditions, which is essential for the development of novel therapies. Traditional transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the individual gene contributions to disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are crucial in determining disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We discover significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can provide context to genetic associations and reveal potential targets that may be overlooked in single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, facilitating insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

            text: ' In the field of genetic studies and functional genomics, understanding gene co-expression patterns is essential for uncovering disease etiology and drug mechanisms. Current methods primarily focus on single genes, overlooking potential interactions that may play a crucial role in disease progression. This manuscript introduces PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. In a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we demonstrate the effectiveness of PhenoPLIER in identifying key players in complex traits. Overall, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through gene modules, providing valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms beyond single-gene strategies.'

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for collaborative analysis. Genes function in concert within specific contexts to perform their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the regulation of expression across different conditions, which is essential for developing novel therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have illuminated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms, contemporary models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on groups of genes with similar expression patterns under identical conditions. We discover that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally critical players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, by incorporating co-expressed gene groups, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and identifies potential targets previously missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for decoding genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby highlighting disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering
              of complex traits

            text: ' In the field of functional genomics, genetic studies have been conducted to understand the underlying mechanisms of diseases and the potential of drug repurposing. However, current research has primarily focused on single-gene strategies, which may not capture the complex interactions between genes that play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our method identifies groups of co-expressed genes, which are significantly associated with diseases in relevant cell types. We demonstrate the accuracy of our approach in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, contextualizing these associations and revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. This approach has the potential to advance our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms, ultimately contributing to the development of more effective therapeutic targets and repurposing of existing drugs.'

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint analysis. Understanding how genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions is crucial for elucidating the influence of these genes on complex traits. This knowledge is vital for discovering novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms, but current models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in the origin and progression of diseases. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on gene modules with similar expression patterns across various conditions. We find that diseases are significantly correlated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Utilizing a CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we discover that functionally critical elements lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, shedding light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

               This study aims to address the gap in current understanding of genetic associations and their role in disease etiology by introducing PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation. The context lies in the recognition that genes often act in concert with each other to perform their functions, and understanding their expression regulation across different conditions is crucial for developing new therapies. Traditionally, transcriptome-wide association studies have focused on individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms; however, modern models of complex trait architecture suggest gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression.               abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is

              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").

              ---
               We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Recognizing that genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, we aim to elucidate how these genes contribute to complex traits with a focus on expression regulation across different conditions. This mechanistic understanding is crucial for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we identify functionally important players that lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and uncovers potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, ultimately facilitating the identification of disease etiologies and drug mechanisms.

          - >-
            We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
            gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
            common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes act in
            concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
            functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
            requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
            different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
            critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide
            association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
            in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
            architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
            play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's
            representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression
            patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are
            significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
            cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
            drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore,
            using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
            functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized
            in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by
            incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
            contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
            missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel
            framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
            gene modules.

            text: ' In the context of genetic associations and gene expression patterns, understanding the mechanisms underlying complex traits is crucial for the development of novel therapies.                Genes work together in specific contexts to carry out their functions, necessitating a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across different conditions for unraveling the influence of these genes on complex traits. This insight is crucial for developing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease initiation and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions.             text: ' In the complex interplay of genes, understanding how they cooperate to influence traits requires a comprehensive view of expression regulation across diverse conditions. This knowledge is essential for developing targeted therapies.               ---
               Genetic studies have provided valuable insights into the etiology of complex diseases and the mechanisms of action for drugs. However, understanding gene-gene interactions in the context of gene expression patterns remains a significant challenge. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across different conditions. We demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using CRISPR screening to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, our work highlights the importance of considering gene co-expression in genetic studies, shedding light on therapeutic targets and facilitating drug repurposing efforts.

              In this paper, we address a critical gap in the literature
              regarding the integration of gene-gene interactions with gene
              expression patterns to better understand disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms. We present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach
              that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
              data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across different conditions. Through extensive
              evaluation, we show that our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover,
              using CRISPR screening to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our work
              has significant implications for the field of genetic studies, as
              it underscores the importance of gene co-expression and its role
              in elucidating therapeutic targets and facilitating drug
              repurposing efforts.

               Genes work in collaboration with each other in specific contexts to carry out their functions. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across various conditions. This insight is crucial for the development of novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been effective in elucidating the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in disease onset and progression. Here, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on groups of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

            text: ' In the context of functional genomics, understanding how genes collaborate in specific scenarios to execute their functions is crucial for decoding the mechanisms behind complex traits and ultimately developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have contributed significantly to identifying individual gene roles in disease-related processes, modern architectural models predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease initiation and progression.             text: ' In the field of genetics, understanding how genes work together in specific contexts is crucial for determining their influence on complex traits. This knowledge is essential for developing new therapies and uncovering disease-relevant mechanisms. Although transcriptome-wide association studies have provided valuable insights into individual gene roles, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across different conditions. Our results demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lacking associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, this study highlights the potential of PhenoPLIER as a powerful tool for understanding gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, and drug repurposing in the context of complex traits.'

              ---
               Genes collaborate in specific contexts to fulfill their functions, necessitating a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across various conditions. This understanding is vital for the development of novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have aided in uncovering individual genes' roles in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is derived from modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally significant players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

              drug-disease pairs and elucidating mechanisms of action. Lastly,
              we discuss the CRISPR screen analysis, which demonstrates the
              prioritization of functionally important players within
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

            text: ' Genetic studies have been crucial in understanding the mechanisms of complex diseases, but existing models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. Functional genomics, particularly transcriptome-wide association studies, has revealed the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms; however, the gap in our understanding lies in how these interactions contribute to complex trait development. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. This novel method not only fills the gap in understanding gene-gene interactions but also contributes to the development of new therapies and a deeper insight into disease etiology and drug mechanisms, ultimately moving the field forward.'

              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.
        - vars:
            test_description: >-
              does not provide an interpretation of the results and their
              implications
            title: >-
              Projecting genetic associations through gene expression patterns
              highlights disease etiology and drug mechanisms
            keywords: >-
              genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
              therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex
              traits
            paragraph: >-
              Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to
              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. It has been shown that
              this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.
